**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

    First Check After Step 6

    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

# DAILY BRIEFING: APRIL 2025

## 1. EXECUTIVE POWER AND GOVERNANCE

### 1.1 Trump's First 100 Days

President Trump's administration has reached its first 100 days with historically low approval ratings. The New Yorker has characterized this period as "One Hundred Days of Ineptitude" [1], while polling indicates Americans, including Republicans, are "losing faith in Trump" [2]. Despite the White House expressing satisfaction with its performance [3], Trump's approval rating has reportedly hit an "80-year low" [4]. The administration is actively dismissing economic concerns as the 100-day milestone approaches [5], even as Americans continue to trust Trump over Democrats according to some metrics [6].

[1] One Hundred Days of Ineptitude, https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2025/05/05/a-hundred-days-of-ineptitude;

[5] Trump’s team brushes off economic concerns ahead of 100-day mark, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/04/27/trump-polling-economic-concerns-00311974;  
[6] Americans Still Trust Donald Trump Over Democrats, https://www.newsweek.com/donald-trump-polling-democrats-republicans-2064747?utm_term=Autofeed&utm_medium=Social&utm_source=Twitter#Echobox=1745762615

### 1.2 Executive Authority and Project 2025

The administration is taking a confrontational stance toward the judiciary, with The Atlantic reporting a warning to judges: "We Will Find You" [1]. Project 2025, the comprehensive conservative policy blueprint, has reportedly become the framework for Trump's second term [2]. Elon Musk's leadership of the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE) is being characterized as "tech-bro Maoism" that has historically led to negative outcomes [3].

[1] Trump Administration to Judges: ‘We Will Find You’, https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2025/04/trump-administration-initimidates-judges/682620/;

## 2. FOREIGN POLICY AND INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS

### 2.1 Russia-Ukraine Conflict

The Russia-Ukraine conflict appears at a critical juncture in negotiations. Senator Rubio has identified the coming week as "very critical" in Russia-Ukraine war talks [1]. President Trump's peace proposals have drawn sharp criticism, with The Telegraph characterizing them as "a total betrayal of Ukraine" [2]. Questions about Trump's relationship with Putin persist, with media questioning whether Trump has "finally realised Putin is playing him" [3].

### 2.2 Global Standing and Territorial Claims

America's global relationships have deteriorated rapidly in the first 100 days, with The New York Times declaring that "100 Days. That’s All It Took to Sever America From the World" [1]. Relations with Canada are particularly strained, with Canadian surveys showing citizens view their relationship with the U.S. as "just as bad as with Russia" [2]. Canadian election discourse now focuses on U.S. relations, with reports that Canadians see the U.S. as "no friend anymore" [3].

The administration has made controversial territorial claims regarding both Greenland and Canada. Greenland's Prime Minister responded that "Greenland is not a piece of property" following what are described as "threats" from Trump [4]. Secretary of State Rubio has addressed Trump's "plans to annex" Canada ahead of Canada's election [5], though Trump denied he was "trolling Canada with 51st state attacks" [6].

## 3. ECONOMIC POLICIES

### 3.1 Tariffs and Trade

The administration's tariff policies are generating significant economic consequences and internal contradictions. Trump is floating new income tax cuts specifically to "ease the bite of tariffs" [1], suggesting acknowledgment that tariffs are creating economic pressure. Cabinet members are publicly at odds, with Reuters reporting that "Trump cabinet members clash on tariff talks with China" [2]. While the Treasury Secretary suggests "there is a path" forward in negotiations [3], Trump has claimed to have "made 200 deals on tariffs" though cabinet members "can't name one" [4].

Tangible economic impacts are emerging, with reports that "a major car manufacturer says it will stop production of this vehicle due to tariffs" [5] and consumer goods are seeing price increases, as "Shein, Temu prices go up today" [6]. The Atlantic presents a dire forecast with "The Coming Economic Nightmare" [7], though some regional perspectives differ, with the Star Tribune reporting that in "rural Minnesota, the pain is worth it" [8].

### 4.1 Democratic Response

Democratic leadership is employing various strategies to counter Republican policies while experiencing internal debates about messaging. Direct action approaches are evident as House Minority Leader Hakeem Jeffries and Senator Cory Booker have organized a sit-in on Capitol steps protesting the GOP budget plan [2][3].

Meanwhile, Senator Bernie Sanders has criticized his own party for lacking "vision for the future" [4] while defending his "Fighting Oligarchy" tour from Democratic criticism, insisting Americans aren't "dumb" and understand what "oligarchy" means [5]. Congressional Republicans face a critical period for implementing President Trump's legislative agenda, with The Hill reporting that the "GOP stares down crucial stretch to pass Trump agenda" [6].

Political tensions are evident at multiple levels of government. CNN reports that "Ron and Casey DeSantis were plotting a political dynasty in Florida. Then came a scandal" [1], indicating disruption to potential succession plans. Pentagon operations appear troubled as "Sen. Jeanne Shaheen says Pete Hegseth has 'created chaos' at the Pentagon" [2]. ### 5.1 Due Process Concerns

Multiple reports indicate escalating tensions over due process rights, particularly for immigrants. ## 6. IMMIGRATION AND CITIZENSHIP

### 6.1 Citizen Children and Family Separation

A major controversy has erupted over U.S. citizen children being sent to Honduras with their undocumented mothers. Multiple outlets report that American children, including "a 4-year-old with cancer," were deported to Honduras [1][2]. Administration officials have offered contradictory responses – the Border Czar maintains "no U.S. citizen child was deported" while acknowledging children were removed with their mothers [3], and Secretary of State Rubio has defended the actions by stating "they can come back" [4].

Simultaneously, Stephen Miller has unveiled what's described as a "bizarre new attack on birthright citizenship" [5], while the Border Czar has stated that "having US-born children does not make people 'immune' from deportation" [6].

### 6.2 Immigration Enforcement

Immigration enforcement actions are intensifying across multiple states. The New York Times reports "ICE Arrests Nearly 800 in Florida in Operation With Local Officers" [1], indicating large-scale coordination between federal and local authorities. In Colorado, "over 100 migrants in the US illegally" were arrested at what's described as "an illegal after-hours nightclub" [2]. In a contrasting case highlighting potential enforcement errors, The Irish Times reports an "Irish woman living legally in US for decades detained after visiting her father in Ireland" [3]. Research from Reason magazine contradicts claims about immigrant criminality, reporting "More Evidence that Immigrants - Including Illegal Ones - Have Much Lower Crime Rates than Natives" [4].

The Atlantic presents a dire forecast with "The Coming Economic Nightmare" [7], though some regional perspectives differ, with the Star Tribune reporting that in "rural Minnesota, the pain is worth it" [8].

Democratic leadership is employing various strategies to counter Republican policies while experiencing internal debates about messaging. Senate Majority Leader Chuck Schumer has declared "I am staying put" regarding leadership transition questions [1]. Meanwhile, Senator Bernie Sanders has criticized his own party for lacking "vision for the future" [4] while defending his "Fighting Oligarchy" tour from Democratic criticism, insisting Americans aren't "dumb" and understand what "oligarchy" means [5]. Congressional Republicans face a critical period for implementing President Trump's legislative agenda, with The Hill reporting that the "GOP stares down crucial stretch to pass Trump agenda" [6].

## 6. Immigration and Citizenship

### 6.1 Citizen Children and Family Separation

A major controversy has erupted over U.S. citizen children being sent to Honduras with their undocumented mothers. Multiple outlets report that American children, including "a 4-year-old with cancer," were deported to Honduras [1][2]. Administration officials have offered contradictory responses – the Border Czar maintains "no U.S. citizen child was deported" while acknowledging children were removed with their mothers [3], and Secretary of State Rubio has defended the actions by stating "they can come back" [4].

Simultaneously, Stephen Miller has unveiled what's described as a "bizarre new attack on birthright citizenship" [5], while the Border Czar has stated that "having US-born children does not make people 'immune' from deportation" [6].

### 6.2 Immigration Enforcement

Immigration enforcement actions are intensifying across multiple states. The New York Times reports "ICE Arrests Nearly 800 in Florida in Operation With Local Officers" [1], indicating large-scale coordination between federal and local authorities. In Colorado, "over 100 migrants in the US illegally" were arrested at what's described as "an illegal after-hours nightclub" [2]. In a contrasting case highlighting potential enforcement errors, The Irish Times reports an "Irish woman living legally in US for decades detained after visiting her father in Ireland" [3]. Research from Reason magazine contradicts claims about immigrant criminality, reporting "More Evidence that Immigrants - Including Illegal Ones - Have Much Lower Crime Rates than Natives" [4].
